## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a chemical concentration A(t), which is the standard setup for kinetic rate laws. With only A and t available, the most likely relationships are autonomous or time-modulated rate laws (orders, reversibility/equilibrium relaxation, autocatalysis, or time-dependent rate constants).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion; linear A vs t until A≈0)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay; exponential A(t))
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction/recombination; 1/A linear in t)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global reaction order over a range of A)
- Generalized (offset) power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * (A + c1)**c2 (handles baseline/shift in effective concentration or measurement offset)
- Reversible/relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (net rate proportional to deviation from equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-form rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating then self-limiting kinetics; sigmoidal A(t))
- Autocatalytic with general order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (c2 - A) (nonlinear autocatalysis or branching kinetics)
- Time-dependent rate constant (exponential deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (catalyst deactivation or fading driving force over time)
- Time-dependent rate constant (ramp): dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * t) * A (slowly changing conditions/temperature program approximated in time)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., photokinetics): dA_dt = -c0 * (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * A (light/chopper modulation or periodic feed)
- Aging/transport-limited slowdown: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + t) (effective rate decreases with time due to fouling or diffusion layer growth)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Monotone consumption with positivity: if A represents a reactant being depleted, dA_dt is typically negative for A>0; models often include an explicit leading minus sign and vanish as A→0.
- Reaction order fingerprint: proportionality dA_dt ∝ A**n implies log(|dA_dt|) vs log(A) is approximately linear with slope n, motivating power-law rate structures.
- Bimolecular/self-reaction behavior: dA_dt ∝ -A**2 produces rapid initial decay and long tails; integrated behavior gives 1/A ~ t, so SR may favor A**2 terms when tails are heavy.
- Approach to equilibrium: dA_dt ∝ -(A - A_eq) indicates exponential relaxation toward A_eq; offsets (A - c1) capture nonzero steady states from reversible reactions or reservoirs.
- Autocatalysis signature: factors like A*(c - A) create a rate that is small at low A, peaks at intermediate A, and returns to zero near a limiting concentration, yielding sigmoidal time courses.
- Non-autonomous kinetics: explicit t-dependence (e.g., exp(-c*t), (c + t)) often represents changing effective rate constants due to catalyst deactivation, mixing warm-up, or transport-layer growth.
- Periodic driving: sin(c*t) modulation in the rate constant reflects periodically varying irradiation or feed; it can imprint oscillations in dA_dt even if A remains smooth.
- Physical bounds/units consistency: polynomial-in-A terms are common because elementary-step kinetics yield rates proportional to products of concentrations; explicit t-only terms typically represent externally imposed protocols rather than intrinsic chemistry.
